# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

API Key Service Interface (pkg/services/apikey/apikey.go)\\nThe `Service` interface defines:\\n- `GetAllAPIKeys()`: Retrieve all API keys for an organization\\n- `AddAPIKey()`: Create new API keys with optional expiration\\n- `GetApiKeyByName()`: Legacy lookup by name\\n- `GetAPIKeyByHash()`: Hash-based lookup for modern tokens\\n- `UpdateAPIKeyLastUsedDate()`: Track API key usage\\n\\n### 3. API Key Service Implementation (pkg/services/apikey/apikeyimpl/apikey.go)\\nImplements the Service interface with database persistence via the SQL store.\\n\\n### 4. API Key Storage (pkg/services/apikey/apikeyimpl/xorm_store.go)\\nThe sqlStore implementation handles:\\n- **AddAPIKey()**: Creates API key with expiration calculation. Modern Token Format (pkg/components/satokengen/tokengen.go)\\nImplements the new API key format:\\n- **Prefix**: \\\"gl\\\" (GrafanaPrefix constant)\\n- **Structure**: `gl<ServiceID>_<Secret>_<Checksum>`\\n- **Hash**: Uses CRC32 checksum validation\\n- **Decode()**: Parses and validates token structure, checking checksum integrity\\n\\n### 9. GRPC Authentication (pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/auth.go)\\nProvides gRPC-specific API key authentication:\\n- `ProvideAuthenticator()`: Creates authenticator with API key and access control services\\n- `tokenAuth()`: Validates Bearer tokens in gRPC metadata\\n- `getSignedInUser()`: Decodes token, looks up API key, validates service account\\n- **Role enforcement**: Requires service account to have Admin role for gRPC access\\n- **Permission loading**: Fetches and caches user permissions from access control service\\n- **Disabled account check**: Denies access to disabled service accounts\\n\\n### 11. Hook System (Hook method in pkg/services/authn/clients/api_key.go)\\nAsynchronously updates last used timestamp:\\n- Runs in background goroutine to avoid blocking requests\\n- Checks if enough time (5 minutes) has passed since last update\\n- Handles panics gracefully\\n\\n### 12. Quota Management (pkg/services/apikey/apikeyimpl/apikey.go)\\nEnforces API key limits:\\n- Global scope quota: `cfg.Quota.Global.ApiKey`\\n- Organization scope quota: `cfg.Quota.Org.ApiKey`\\n- Registers quota reporter with quota service\\n\\n### Key Security Features:\\n\\n1. **Multiple validation layers**: API keys are validated at both HTTP and gRPC levels\\n2. **Expiration enforcement**: API keys with `Expires` timestamp are automatically rejected if expired\\n3. **Revocation support**: Keys can be revoked via `IsRevoked` flag\\n4. **Organization scoping**: Keys are bound to specific organizations, preventing cross-org access\\n5. **Service account binding**: Modern API keys must be associated with service accounts, replacing legacy plain keys\\n6. **Hash-based validation**: Uses bcrypt hashing (via util.EncodePassword) for secure key storage\\n7. **Token integrity**: New token format includes CRC32 checksum to detect tampering\\n8. **Role-based access**: Service accounts using API keys can have different roles (Viewer, Editor, Admin)\\n9. **Permission synchronization**: Permissions are fetched from the access control service for fine-grained authorization\\n10. **Usage tracking**: API key last used timestamp enables auditing and security monitoring\\n\"\n}\n",
